    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer5801381747151736860">It’s 2002, a year after 9/11. It’s an extremely turbulent time politically, but especially so for someone like Shirin, a sixteen-year-old Muslim girl who’s tired of being stereotyped.<br/><br/>Shirin is never surprised by how horrible people can be. She’s tired of the rude stares, the degrading comments - even the physical violence - she endures as a result of her race, her religion</span>
  <span id="freeText5801381747151736860" style="display:none">It’s 2002, a year after 9/11. It’s an extremely turbulent time politically, but especially so for someone like Shirin, a sixteen-year-old Muslim girl who’s tired of being stereotyped.<br /><br />Shirin is never surprised by how horrible people can be. She’s tired of the rude stares, the degrading comments - even the physical violence - she endures as a result of her race, her religion, and the hijab she wears every day. So she’s built up protective walls and refuses to let anyone close enough to hurt her. Instead, she drowns her frustrations in music and spends her afternoons break-dancing with her brother.<br /><br />But then she meets Ocean James. He’s the first person in forever who really seems to want to get to know Shirin. It terrifies her - they seem to come from two irreconcilable worlds - and Shirin has had her guard up for so long that she’s not sure she’ll ever be able to let it down.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5801381747151736860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.latimes.com/books/la-et-jc-tahereh-mafi-20180222-story.html'>http://www.latimes.com/books/la-et-jc...</a><br/><br/>“I'm going to get asked this question so much because she falls in love with this white boy, Ocean, and I'm ma<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.latimes.com/books/la-et-jc-tahereh-mafi-20180222-story.html">http://www.latimes.com/books/la-et-jc...</a><br /><br />“I'm going to get asked this question so much because she falls in love with this white boy, Ocean, and I'm married to a white man. The obvious answer is no: I met my husband [the writer Ransom Riggs] as an adult, and we were very different people than this character and her love interest. But Ocean's personality is inspired quite a bit by my husband's personality. And there are certain conversations that they have that I've absolutely had with my husband, things that they have to face together, like the complications of being in an interracial relationship.”<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_2546499909" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2546499909" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2546499909?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=muslim-rep">muslim-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=own-voices">own-voices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=poc-rep">poc-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-friends-to-lovers">trope-friends-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2546499909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13611137434602913725">Y’all mind if I cry because if you’d told 16 year-old me that one day I’ll read a NYT best-selling book where a Muslim Hijabi teen gets her own coming of age story and her own big romance instead of being the token (stereotyped) minority character or some cultural prop used only to further the writer’s favorite white girl…it would have made a world of difference.<br/><br/><strong>
  <u>So, what’s this book about?</u>
</strong><br/><br/>Shirin could scarcely remember what her life had been like, back before the events of 9/11 had made of i</span>
  <span id="freeText13611137434602913725" style="display:none">Y’all mind if I cry because if you’d told 16 year-old me that one day I’ll read a NYT best-selling book where a Muslim Hijabi teen gets her own coming of age story and her own big romance instead of being the token (stereotyped) minority character or some cultural prop used only to further the writer’s favorite white girl…it would have made a world of difference.<br /><br /><strong>
  <u>So, what’s this book about?</u>
</strong><br /><br />Shirin could scarcely remember what her life had been like, back before the events of 9/11 had made of it the zoo of terrors it was now: her life becoming scraps that had been talked over so many times that they’d worn and frayed, every conversation with her peers and teachers like walking through thorny brambles of islamophobia and xenophobia, and a horrifying incident on her way home back from school that was tucked deep inside layers and layers of remembering and that left the old cold fear—the constant companion of a Hijabi Muslim in a post-9/11 America—alive within her.<br /><br />It didn’t help that her immigrant parents moved around each year for better job opportunities and better school district—every new place only a pause in the long stretch of Shirin’s solitude. Shirin copes by withdrawing too far into herself to be permeable to the world’s cruelty, still and quiet and determined to suffer alone. Until one day, her brother introduces her to his breakdancing crew, and it was the feeling of being lost and alone and then suddenly neither. Then, she meets Ocean, the school’s golden boy, who starts wearing at her shell with every fleeting conversation and smile and act of kindness.<br /><br />Shirin’s aloofness used to be like armor, but she’d lost it, and without it, she’d found herself defenseless against the hope trying to well up in her.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“If the decision you’ve made has brought you closer to humanity, then you’ve done the right thing.” </em>
</blockquote><br /><br />I’ve always believed that works of fiction are reflections of the people who had woven and spun them, and are flecked with little truths, little intrusions of reality into fiction. Mafi, A Muslim Iranian-American author, said that this was <a href="https://twitter.com/TaherehMafi/status/966721299396444162" rel="nofollow noopener">the most autobiographical novel</a> she has written. No wonder, then, that <em>A Large Expanse of Sea</em> shone bright with sincerity and the same vitality her characters radiated, in spite of the shadow that their circumstances had grown over them.<br /><br />Everything about this book fitted right into the hollows of my heart. When I first heard that this is the story of a fellow teen Muslim, my hope came so sharp that I didn’t dare speak it. My joy, now, is inarticulate—I could never quite explain the blaze of connection, the feeling of being seen and set apart that planted seeds of gratitude that would come to flower.<br /><br />This book had me laughing and crying at 10% of the e-book. I read it in one sitting. <strong><em>A Large Expanse of Sea</em> is heartbreaking in its realness</strong>, but I felt its sorrow absorb some of my own. Mafi digs deep into the story’s timeless themes and pulls up something nourishing from the roots. Not only does she relay all of the Muslim teen’s many worries and concerns, she also renders them universal in their specificity—by capturing the richness of relationships among family and friends, Shirin’s familiar romp through teenagedom, and even her love for fashion, music and dancing.<br /><br />That's the thing I relished most about this book. Yes, it is starring a Muslim Hijabi teen and it does a successful job of highlighting her religious beliefs and her cultural history and struggles, but it also shows Shirin as an average teen whose religion is just<em> a part</em> of what makes up the smart, funny and kind person she is. <strong>It’s what makes it one of the realest and most relatable books that I’ve ever read</strong>—so many aspects of Shirin’s journey, as a Muslim and as a teen, could be so easily woven among my own.<br /><br />Speaking of which, I <em>LOVE</em> Shirin.<br /><br /><strong>The feel of her isolation, cold and sharp, spills onto paper.</strong> My gut was knotting with sympathetic misery at seeing her being ostracized, isolated, wearier than she’d been the day before, but always hiding it, deciding things were fine just so she’d feel like she’d gotten her bearing again. Shirin is constantly throwing out so many verbal smoke bombs, obfuscating some very important things that are happening behind them. Like how much it stung that her classmates saw only what they wanted to see. Not a girl or a woman or someone in between. They didn’t see Shirin’s loneliness or fear or courage, let alone her humanity. They saw only difference, danger, obscenity. Like how it didn’t matter that she was just as American as they were, that her only crime was trying to peacefully live her religious beliefs.<br /><br />When you’re a minority, those are the worries you grow up with, and they are dulled by familiarity. But there are always new worries, because there is new ignorance, new hate. . . and new hope, and those are neither familiar nor dull. <strong>This book might be set in the early 2000s, but it feels too timely and too relevant under the current political climate.</strong><br /><br /><em>A Large Expanse of Sea</em> also gently touches first love, spiriting you back to those wild and poignant roller coaster days of young love. Mafi takes well-worn tropes and filters them through the lens of a culture that is seldom represented and humanized to turn them into something all kinds of new.<br /><br />Shirin falls for Ocean, and the warmth in her that Ocean reciprocates her feelings and would risk everyone’s disapproval, is weighted with the understanding that they would hurt him for it. And because it would have been easier to convince herself that there were some motive, some sort of revenge in the works, or some other manner of scheming, Shirin layers cynicism atop her longing and does everything to drive him away.<br /><br />Although Ocean doesn’t initially understand why Shirin would let the gap in their cultures and interests become a chasm, <b>he soon realizes just how blithely unaware he was of the full power of his white privilege</b>, and the bubble he’s been cocooned in quickly evaporates. However much Ocean wanted to be like a prince charging up to the maiden’s tower to save her, the reality was: he was so mad with longing that he forgot his sword and was slain by the dragon before he even got near her. The dragon in this case was a battalion of hate-ravaged classmates, family and teachers, and the good nature and kindness Ocean wielded was not enough a weapon. <em>A Large Expanse of Sea</em> certainly doesn’t shy away from the challenges and complexities intercultural relationships face. It asks hard questions at every turn, offering only the uncertainty of its answers.<br /><br />But I think the greatest takeaway from this book and the lesson that is so central to Shirin's arc is to not let the tangle of fury and grief and despair define your life and your interactions with the world. It's easy sometimes to let the repeated exposure to cruelty parch away the belief that there is goodness in the world still, and this book was a nice reminder of that.<br /><br />My one real complaint about <em>A Large Expanse of Sea</em> is that all its climaxes peak at once, in a whirlwind of tension and revelation. I think a little more build-up might have led to a smoother conclusion. Another small quibble is the second love interest, Yusef, who doesn’t quite step whole into the page. Yusuf is Lebanese-American, and he shares a lot of values and interests with Shirin. His character had so much brimming potential, yet he was not given enough page time. It’s strange to admit this because I usually hate the barest whispers of a love triangle, but I could have really gotten behind this one.<br /><br />Anyway, with all that being said, so successful is this book in every other aspect that the aforementioned quibbles only struck me as minor bumps in the road. And overall,<em> A Large Expanse of Sea</em> is a beautiful read that alternates between soul-wrenching, haunting and entrancing.<br /><br /><blockquote>✨ <a href="http://amzn.eu/9Jnbkf3" rel="nofollow noopener">wishlist</a> ✨ <a href="https://runawaywithdreamthieves.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ✨ <a href="https://twitter.com/kzabrekker" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ✨ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ✨</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="13611137434602913725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2783146287275924831">One of the best contemporary books I've ever read, and hands-down the best YA on what it means to be a Muslim American post 9/11. Tahereh Mafi pulls no punches, spares no feelings and tells the absolute truth and it is beautiful, rare and heartbreaking. If there's one book you read this year, make it this one. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2564885610" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2564885610" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2564885610?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30604861-emma-giordano?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2564885610" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer583113034574665788">4.5 Stars! Review to come.<br/><br/>CW: islamophobia & xenophobia</span>

<div id="review_2315877060" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2315877060" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2315877060?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=favs-of-2018">favs-of-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=sent-from-pub">sent-from-pub</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2315877060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11305693688862805077"><b>October 2018</b> <br/>Updating with my full thoughts now that the book is out! I wrote all of this down when I first read it in May.<br/><br/>I was nervous starting this book because the first 25% of this lays a lot of groundwork and there’s a lot of telling instead of showing. Despite this, I was highlighting paragraphs basically every other page because Shirin’s experiences and anger born from them was so powerful. This book cuts the crap from Shatter Me & Furthermore’s writing style and says it how it is. Gone </span>
  <span id="freeText11305693688862805077" style="display:none"><b>October 2018</b> <br />Updating with my full thoughts now that the book is out! I wrote all of this down when I first read it in May.<br /><br />I was nervous starting this book because the first 25% of this lays a lot of groundwork and there’s a lot of telling instead of showing. Despite this, I was highlighting paragraphs basically every other page because Shirin’s experiences and anger born from them was so powerful. This book cuts the crap from Shatter Me &amp; Furthermore’s writing style and says it how it is. Gone are the flowery paragraphs of images and metaphors, but they’re replaced by hard-hitting and steel edged descriptions of Shirin’s real life. It’s different and it’s jarring, but it fits the story. I’m not even exaggerating when I say that probably 50% of this ebook’s text is highlighted. From powerful moments to funny, relatable moments to important moments to cute moments, I was glued onto the pages. <br /><br />I LOVED Shirin’s relationship with her brother, Navid. Their bond was endearing and I liked how he was her mentor and cheered her up and stuck up for her and was the reason she got into break dancing. He was definitely my favorite side character!<br /><br />I can’t put my finger on it, but this book just.... works. It was fast to read. I haven’t lived a life anywhere near Shirin’s, but being in her head made sense. I understood her feelings. I understood her fears. I sympathized with her so much that my heart hurt. I was rooting for her the entire book, and her transformation and self-actualization was such an engrossing journey. <br /><br />The reason why I took a star off is because the relationship is melodramatic to the point of being cliche. Shirin deals with racism and xenophobia and bigotry, and Ocean deals with..... not wanting to be on the basketball team. It felt like a flat plot point that’s a totally overused trope. The stakes were so low because it felt too cliché and the conflict of this book reminded me of High School Musical. I don't want this to look like I'm minimizing the actual events because clearly Shirin prevailing and asserting her worth in that situation was still such a powerful read, but I wish Ocean's conflict that drives the emotional climax of this book could have been designed to be less.... generic. <br /><br />Nevertheless, this is a once in a lifetime book. Whatever small writing or plot issues I have with it makes up in the fact that I haven’t read anything as important and eye-opening as this before. Its unparalleled honesty had me throwing my fist in the hair during some scenes and wiping away tears in others. It’s a stand-out book of 2018, and definitely an exception you should make if you aren't a fan of YA contemporary. Please please please support this book and the author behind it because she and the book deserve the world &lt;3 <br /><br /><b>May 2018</b><br />I don't think I've read a book in one sitting since high school. But here I am at 8 AM, staring at the acknowledgments page of my eARC. Wow. I’m not even exaggerating when I say that probably 50% of this ebook’s text is highlighted. From powerful moments to funny, relatable moments to important moments to cute moments, I was glued onto the pages. I haven’t lived a life anywhere near Shirin’s, but being in her head made sense. I understood her fears and I sympathized for her so much. I was rooting for her the entire book, and her transformation and self-actualization was such an engrossing journey. This is a once in a lifetime book. Whatever small writing or plot issues I have with it makes up in the fact that I haven’t read anything as important and singularly eye-opening as this before. Its unparalleled honesty had me throwing my fist in the air during some scenes and wiping away tears in others. It’s a stand-out book of 2018. <br /><br />I'll update with detailed thoughts closer to the book's release but I can't wait for the cover reveal of this, and Muslim reviewers and teens deserve to get their hands on this. It's such a vital story for the YA community written so honestly and captivatingly.<br /><br /><b>May 2018</b><br />my craving for this book is so palpable that my chest aches. i'm so ready for it but at the same time, i'm so, so not. either way, if this book isn't a #1 nyt bestseller then i'm gonna personally scream its name from the rooftops, mark my words.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11305693688862805077" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2305934856" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2305934856" />
    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2305934856?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781405292603" href="/book/show/40309051-a-very-large-expanse-of-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=author-of-colour">author-of-colour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=characters-of-colour">characters-of-colour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=library-reads">library-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2305934856" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14905290789582199981">I’m finding it difficult forming words and putting it onto paper here. I felt a whole range of emotions reading this book and it became exhausting to read. In a good way. <br/><br/>This is a semi-autobiographical story, set in America, following the tragedy of 9/11, where we follow Shirin trying to navigate a world where Islamophobia is rampant, her existence questionable. The hate is apparent and because she stands out due to her hijab, she’s on the constant end of receiving racist remarks and at times, </span>
  <span id="freeText14905290789582199981" style="display:none">I’m finding it difficult forming words and putting it onto paper here. I felt a whole range of emotions reading this book and it became exhausting to read. In a good way. <br /><br />This is a semi-autobiographical story, set in America, following the tragedy of 9/11, where we follow Shirin trying to navigate a world where Islamophobia is rampant, her existence questionable. The hate is apparent and because she stands out due to her hijab, she’s on the constant end of receiving racist remarks and at times, abuse. <br /><br />Her anger was palpable and rightly so. The hurt and the constant ridicule she was facing left no room for her to breathe, no space for her to sort through her emotions. She locks herself up from the outside world and her own feelings in order to protect herself. There was no choice but to have a guard up. It was a lot to take in. The writing forced me to feel it all. It was suffocating. <br /><br />Amidst all this, she finds comfort in books and break-dancing, whilst also trying to sort through her emotions as she begins falling for a boy. <br /><br />I think reading this book made it quite clear the lack of Muslim literature we have access to. They are scattered and very few and far in between. Authentic Muslim voices in the West are rarely heard through any form of media and if they are, they aren’t positive. And the books that are being published now is a controlled narrative by a publishing world that is still very white. <br /><br />It makes you wonder why. Is the lack thereof due to fear? That it won’t be marketable? Believing that it won’t resonate with other readers because a connection won’t be formed? But isn’t that the whole point of books? For us to be exposed to something slightly alien and for others to at least understand that these experiences are out there and are just as valid even if you might not agree? That the point isn’t the come to a agreement, but to acknowledge it exists. Our narratives, in its plethora and all its colours, matters. <br /><br />These stories might not represent our faith but they represent our people, in all it’s glory and wonder and failures and that was Shirin’s story to me. I could relate to her anger. I know I have walked around with this look on my face and my guard up just so people would not approach me and/or have the nerve to comment on my attire and my beliefs. My guard had to be up just so I could be prepared for any kind of attack, even if the threat wasn’t there. <br />And don’t get me started on the days where the news would report on a terrorist attack. My ‘stank face’ would come out even more. <br /><br />It’s not easy holding on to your faith in a world that refuses to understand your world. But we fight through it, because this faith of our means something to us. <br /><br />I hope from now on the publishing world not only acknowledge their failure at providing us with authentic stories, but are trying their best to accommodating those voices that are demanding it. Shit needs to change. <br />Enough is enough.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14905290789582199981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2519881017" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2519881017" />
    <a title="Hamad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad"><img alt="Hamad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577880699p2/54464244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2519881017?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hamad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hamad" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad">Hamad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2519881017" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5137880039101297215">This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2018/09/10/arc-review-a-very-large-expanse-of-sea/' rel='nofollow noopener'>@The Book Prescription</a><br/><br/><b>Actual Rating: 3.5 stars</b><br/><br/> <i>“I was stuck in another small town, trapped in another universe populated by the kind of people who’d only ever seen faces like mine on their evening news, and I hated it.</i><br/><br/>🌟 I should start this review by making one point very clear: I am an Arab Muslim Palestinian guy, so I do understand this book more than most readers will.<br/><br/>🌟 I like that Tahereh is trying all different kid of things like MG and</span>
  <span id="freeText5137880039101297215" style="display:none">This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2018/09/10/arc-review-a-very-large-expanse-of-sea/" rel="nofollow noopener">@The Book Prescription</a><br /><br /><b>Actual Rating: 3.5 stars</b><br /><br /> <i>“I was stuck in another small town, trapped in another universe populated by the kind of people who’d only ever seen faces like mine on their evening news, and I hated it.</i><br /><br />🌟 I should start this review by making one point very clear: I am an Arab Muslim Palestinian guy, so I do understand this book more than most readers will.<br /><br />🌟 I like that Tahereh is trying all different kid of things like MG and contemporary. I was disappointed by Restore me as many of you know but this book was totally different and it restored my faith in Tahereh’s writing.<br /><br />🌟 Speaking of which, the writing is different from the Shatter me series, while there it was whimsical and poetic, here it was normal with a tone that is fitting for a contemporary. I think this may be a good book for those who did not like the shatter me series and are willing to give Tahereh a second chance.<br /><br />🌟 Also the story is discussing very important subjects and I think it will be quite popular as THUG did. (But I expect a little bit less popularity). It talks about Islam and xenophobia mainly, which I will get back to later in this review.<br /><br />🌟 Also, Tahereh made this personal by including break-dancing and sports and high school stuff. Now the reviews have been mostly positive but I need to shed light on some things that bothered me.<br /><br />🌟 While the book started with the sensitive topics and I thought it was great, it quickly veered toward a romance which in my opinion was not needed. Or at least, should not have been the focus of the story, the romance should have been used to move the plot forward instead of becoming sort of the plot.<br /><br />🌟 The Break-dancing part: I really love destorying the stereotype about Muslim Girls and that they can’t do (and actually be good) at anything they want to as Music and sports and writing ..etc. I just wish there was more focus on this and more showing instead of telling. We have Shirin who was an amateur at break-dancing and then trained and became good and there was not much showing us that because Shirin was pre-occupied with the love interest as mentioned earlier. I need to mention Navid and the other guys who were so funny and protective of Shirin and made the story better.<br /><br />🌟 Now to the spicy part that annoyed me a bit and made the final saying in my rating. The Islam part!<br />When you want to write a book like this then you have to be very objective and to put personal ideals and thoughts apart. There are some things that are open to discussion in Islam and are personal preferences and some things are simply not.<br />To explain further: no one can discuss if praying in Islam is a must or not because it clearly is. But a man shaking a woman’s hand is debatable, Personally I do shake hands and don’t mind while some other guys prefer not to and to each his own.<br />Why I am saying this? Because there were some inaccuracies and they may give a false ideas to those who are looking for answers. It does not matter where and when you were born (As some readers may say it is due to Tahereh being raised up in the west) some things are not acceptable and Shirin clearly did them and even defended her choices.<br /><br />🌟 Summary: This book which is like a semi-Autobiography discussed serious subjects. It had a modern and light voice to it and was easy to read. It could have been better with improved Islam Rep, more break-dancing and less romance. Still a good book that I can recommend to people.<br /><br />🌟 Prescription: To those who find the synopsis intriguing but will not take everything in this for granted.<br /><br />BR this with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/28683811-noura-khalid-theperksofbeingnoura" rel="nofollow noopener">Noura of ARCs</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5137880039101297215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2418029732" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2418029732" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2418029732?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=otp">otp</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-ebooks">owned-ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2418029732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11154655693851233911">If you know my reading tastes much, you’ll already know that I almost never pick up a contemporary novel unless it involves one of three things: diverse rep, a heartbreaking learning experience (for the reader <i>or</i> the characters), or a romance so sweet and lovable that I can’t help but get sucked in. It’s really rare that I find a book that has all <b>three</b> of those traits, yet here we are.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I didn’t understand how anyone could be so violently angry with me for something I hadn’t done, so much</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText11154655693851233911" style="display:none">If you know my reading tastes much, you’ll already know that I almost never pick up a contemporary novel unless it involves one of three things: diverse rep, a heartbreaking learning experience (for the reader <i>or</i> the characters), or a romance so sweet and lovable that I can’t help but get sucked in. It’s really rare that I find a book that has all <b>three</b> of those traits, yet here we are.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I didn’t understand how anyone could be so violently angry with me for something I hadn’t done, so much so that they’d feel justified in assaulting me in broad daylight as I walked down the street. I didn’t want to understand it. But there it was.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />This is my first Tahereh Mafi read (unless you count the few chapters of <i>Shatter Me</i> I’ve read so far), and I could not put it down. I sat down late one night with the intentions of reading a couple of chapters before bed, and the next thing I knew, it was 4am and I had just finished it and <b>could not stop crying</b> from this mixture of sadness and grief and happiness and love and just… <i>everything.</i> <b>Tahereh Mafi gave me literally every possible emotion I could imagine while reading this gorgeous story.</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I worried that if I spoke or screamed my anger would grip both sides of my open mouth and rip me in half. So I said nothing.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />First and foremost, it’s a story inspired by Tahereh Mafi’s own high school life: our protagonist Shirin is a high schooler in the wake of 9/11, shortly after the event occurred, which isn’t an easy place to be when you’re a Muslim girl, the daughter of Persian immigrants who fought and worked their way to the US from Iran, and a <i>hijabi.</i> On top of all of that, her parents move her and her brother Navid constantly, and where the story picks up, Shirin is yet again the new girl whose classmates won’t look past her scarf and skin color long enough to learn more about her: like the music she loves, or the immense value she places on her family and their Persian cooking, or her secret affinity for break dancing.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I was stuck in another small town, trapped in another universe populated by the kind of people who’d only ever seen faces like mine on their evening news, and I hated it.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Obviously, as a white woman from the US, with no immigration in my recent ancestors and no religious affiliations, I can’t begin to speak for the representation in this book; however, Tahereh explains in her author’s note that every bit of it is own-voice (even the break dancing!), and many of my Muslim friends have been raving about this book already. <b>(If you have an own-voice review for this book, please let me know and I’ll boost your review! ♥)</b> What I <i>can</i> say, though, is that Shirin is such an incredible character and I loved the representation. I learned so much, but more than that, I was given just a tiny little glimpse into what it must be like to be a Muslim in a xenophobic, Islamophobic world, and it broke my heart a million times over.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “I’m just—I’m sick and tired of trying to explain to the world why racism is bad, okay? Why is that my job?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />There’s also a running theme of Shirin discussing not only how racism affects her in obvious ways, such as the assailants who attacked her right after 9/11, but also in microaggressions and people being careless despite thinking they had good intentions. It’s so easy to understand why Shirin walks around with walls of thick stone surrounding her, and why it’s so hard for her to let people in—because even the people that seem “good” usually end up hurting her, whether it’s through ignorance or malevolence.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>My parents had made sure to make an entirely separate, six-course meal for this friend of mine who’d never tried Persian food before, and they’d sat there and stared at him as he ate, and every time he said he liked what he’d eaten they would look up at me and beam, proud as peacocks, finding in Ocean further proof that Persian people had invented only the best things, including the best food.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />I also can safely say that the storytelling itself is among the best of any YA contemporaries I’ve ever read. In between the anger and hurt Shirin lives in, she’s <i>funny,</i> clever, and just an all-around enjoyable narrator. Her family is so lovable (her brother and parents made me smile constantly), the descriptions of food had my mouth watering all the time, and most of all, <b>the romance is one of the sweetest, purest, most adorable contemporary ships I’ve ever seen in my life.</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>But I knew Ocean and I were thinking the same thing. I could feel it in the subtle shifts of his body. I heard it in his sudden, slow inhalations. In the tightness in his breath when he leaned in and whispered, “Where the hell did you come from?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />I literally highlighted page upon page of Shirin and Ocean’s interactions, no shame. I laughed, I blushed, I <i>cried</i> so many times over how sweet they are together. Ocean is a rare YA love interest who can ride the fine line between being incredibly sweet and eloquent, without ever seeming overly scripted or unrealistic. <b>Shirin and Ocean are the kind of couple that makes us believe in the endless weight of young love, whether we’re in our teens or long past them.</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>But I had never, ever touched someone and felt like this: like I was holding electricity inside of me.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />I honestly feel like I can’t possibly gush enough about <i>A Very Large Expanse of Sea.</i> It is one of my favorite reads of the year so far, and I know it’s the type of story I’ll go back to over and over again because it won’t get old. Tahereh Mafi has earned me as a lifetime fan with this story, I have no doubt, and after reading this, I can’t wait to dive back into the <i>Shatter Me</i> world and then read everything else she ever writes, too.<br /><br /><i>All quotes come from an advance copy and may not match the final release. Thank you so much to HarperTeen for providing me with this ARC in exchange for an honest review!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11154655693851233911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11182406289947478498">oh wow. im surprised by how much i actually enjoyed this! much more than i thought i would, considering i really had no expectations for it whatsoever. but it wasnt always upward positivity. <br/><br/>actually, my feelings whilst reading this would look similar to a square root symbol - √ - if i were to graph it. it began with pretty neutral feelings (like i said, no expectations), before plunging in great frustration (i found the main character to be extremely unlikable and insufferable) but then pleasan</span>
  <span id="freeText11182406289947478498" style="display:none">oh wow. im surprised by how much i actually enjoyed this! much more than i thought i would, considering i really had no expectations for it whatsoever. but it wasnt always upward positivity. <br /><br />actually, my feelings whilst reading this would look similar to a square root symbol - √ - if i were to graph it. it began with pretty neutral feelings (like i said, no expectations), before plunging in great frustration (i found the main character to be extremely unlikable and insufferable) but then pleasantly and steadily inclined (i forgave the main character for her hostility towards literally everyone, eventually coming to understand it, and i enjoyed seeing her and her BF grow in the face of adversity).<br /><br />overall, this a pretty wholesome story. i do wish i could have formed more of an attachment with shirin, but she kept everyone at arms length (which i guess included me) and i couldnt really find any sort of fondness for her. but i do like the message of this story and im excited to see if mafi writes more contemporary stories in the future! <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_2566834000" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2566834000" />
    <a title="BernLuvsBooks " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3087404-bernluvsbooks"><img alt="BernLuvsBooks " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585010050p2/3087404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2566834000?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BernLuvsBooks " class="user" itemprop="url" name="BernLuvsBooks " href="/user/show/3087404-bernluvsbooks">BernLuvsBooks </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=ya-books">ya-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=fave-reads">fave-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2566834000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9620208721472785238"><u>
  <i>
    <b>A Very Large Expanse of Sea</b>
  </i>
</u> by Tahereh Mafi broke me while simultaneously filling my mind, soul and heart with vast emotions all at the same time.<br/><br/>This book deserves all the stars for the raw emotion it made me feel. Tahereh Mafi's voice was so honest - Shirin was funny, intelligent, clever and so angry. She was the perfect narrator. My heart bled for her. Shirin's pain was so real - I wanted to hug her fiercely. The story follows Shirin as her family moves to yet another new city. Sh</span>
  <span id="freeText9620208721472785238" style="display:none"><u>
  <i>
    <b>A Very Large Expanse of Sea</b>
  </i>
</u> by Tahereh Mafi broke me while simultaneously filling my mind, soul and heart with vast emotions all at the same time.<br /><br />This book deserves all the stars for the raw emotion it made me feel. Tahereh Mafi's voice was so honest - Shirin was funny, intelligent, clever and so angry. She was the perfect narrator. My heart bled for her. Shirin's pain was so real - I wanted to hug her fiercely. The story follows Shirin as her family moves to yet another new city. She deals with daily racism, hate and degrading comments from being a Muslim teen post 9/11. I adored her fierceness, her strength and her vulnerability. Tahereh wrote from her own personal experiences, creating a truly powerful and inspirational character in Shirin. I truly loved watching her grow throughout the book. Her self awakening was beautiful. <br /><br />The romance between Ocean and Shirin was impossible not to get caught up in. Could he have been any more swoon worthy? He was the perfect complement to Shirin's fierceness. His innocence, tenderness and honesty were exactly what she needed to pierce through the armor she had built up around herself. Their relationship built up slowly and I was enthralled with every angsty moment of it. It made me feel like a love-sick teenager all over again. Their's was not an easy road to love - it was bumpy, heartbreaking and painful at times. Yet, it was wholeheartedly genuine, sweet and utterly undeniable. <br /><br />To say this book was a roller coaster ride of emotion would be an understatement! I laughed, I cried, I gasped out loud and I definitely cringed at some of the racism and bigotry Shirin endured. Did I mention there was breakdancing?! There is and it was a wonderful, unexpected addition for this Bronx native! <b><u><i>A Very Large Expanse of Sea</i></u> was an emotional, beautifully written story - in short it's the kind of story you know you won't soon forget.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="9620208721472785238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2640645842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer33139895518637205">Tahereh Mafi better write more YA contemporary romance novels in the future because this one was absolutely moving and memorable. It’s been a long time since I fell so hard for a YA love interest but Ocean was just EVERYTHING. Oh my goodness. It’s both an uplifting and saddening story at times. It’s beautiful and makes you believe in true love, but the heroine experiences racism throughout the story and the constant need to educate people weighs on her. There’s a bit too much angst for me to giv</span>
  <span id="freeText33139895518637205" style="display:none">Tahereh Mafi better write more YA contemporary romance novels in the future because this one was absolutely moving and memorable. It’s been a long time since I fell so hard for a YA love interest but Ocean was just EVERYTHING. Oh my goodness. It’s both an uplifting and saddening story at times. It’s beautiful and makes you believe in true love, but the heroine experiences racism throughout the story and the constant need to educate people weighs on her. There’s a bit too much angst for me to give it five stars but I finished it in less than four hours and I couldn’t recommend it enough to those who are looking for a realistic story that, yes, isn’t easy to swallow but will ultimately add meaning to your day. </span>

<div id="review_2576032067" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2576032067" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2576032067?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2576032067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1767381670121669505">I read for a number of different reasons. I read for relaxation, for entertainment, for escape. I read to be provoked into thought or action, I read to feel, and sometimes my funny bone or my tear ducts need a good workout. And sometimes, I read to learn.<br/><br/>The ideal book is a combination of at least a few of these, which was one of the reasons I enjoyed Tahereh Mafi's newest novel, <b>
  <i>A Very Large Expanse of Sea</i>
</b>. I empathized with the characters and found the story emotional and appealing, but I </span>
  <span id="freeText1767381670121669505" style="display:none">I read for a number of different reasons. I read for relaxation, for entertainment, for escape. I read to be provoked into thought or action, I read to feel, and sometimes my funny bone or my tear ducts need a good workout. And sometimes, I read to learn.<br /><br />The ideal book is a combination of at least a few of these, which was one of the reasons I enjoyed Tahereh Mafi's newest novel, <b>
  <i>A Very Large Expanse of Sea</i>
</b>. I empathized with the characters and found the story emotional and appealing, but I also learned a little more about what the world was like for a teenage Persian girl in the months after 9/11.<br /><br />Shirin is 16 years old. One thing she and her family have become tremendously skilled at is moving. It seems like any time they start to feel settled, her parents decide it's time to move again, ostensibly to find an even better life for Shirin and her older brother, Navid. What they don't understand is how the world—and especially high school—can be so horribly cruel to a teenage Persian girl who wears a headscarf. (Given all of the horrible torture and turmoil her parents faced to escape from Iran and give their children a chance at happiness and success, they're not tremendously moved by Shirin's tales of cruelty, ridicule, and occasional violence.)<br /><br />"These, the regular injections of poison I was gifted from strangers, were definitely the worst things about wearing a headscarf. But the best thing about it was that my teachers couldn't see me listening to music."<br /><br />In an effort to just get through the days, Shirin immerses herself in music, which helps her express her outrage and her loneliness, even if it's mostly self-imposed. But her favorite activity is breakdancing with her brother, and when he and his friends start a breakdancing club in school, she can't wait to be a part of it. She can have her protective walls and still learn the moves she's watched on old VHS tapes for years.<br /><br />Then she meets Ocean, a fellow student who becomes her lab partner in biology class. He isn't willing to be pushed away by Shirin's immediate need to keep everyone beyond arm's length. He actually wants to know about what it's like to be Persian, not because he thinks she's an oddity, but because he's actually interested. But more than that, he's interested in her. And Shirin just can't have that. Even as she finds herself thinking more and more about Ocean, and wanting to be with him, she already knows how everything will turn out, and she doesn't want to put herself or him through that.<br /><br />"It took a lot out of me to put up the walls that kept me safe from heartbreak, and at the end of every day I felt so withered by the emotional exertion that sometimes my whole body felt shaky."<br /><br />When she decides that she can't live her life angry all the time, without letting anyone in, she lets herself be vulnerable. But even world-weary Shirin isn't prepared for the way people will behave. The fickleness of human behavior, the fear, the ignorance, the obsessions, become almost too much for her to bear, but she really has nowhere to turn. How could the possibility of love be worth all of this?<br /><br />This was a tremendously affecting, beautifully written, thought-provoking (and anger-provoking) novel. I read the entire book in a day, and was simultaneously moved, outraged, saddened, horrified, embarrassed, and utterly hooked. All too often we make judgments about a person because of how they behave, or what they look like, or what their beliefs are, and it's amazing how often we lose the true person we're judging.<br /><br />I had never read any of Mafi's books before, although I've always wanted to. Even though I know her other books are very different from this one, clearly she is an incredible storyteller, because she had me staying up late to finish this, and I can't stop thinking about Shirin and Ocean. What a fascinating and beautiful story this was.<br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>, or check out my list of the best books I read in 2017 at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2018/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2017.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2018/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2017.html</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1767381670121669505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2305067737" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2305067737" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2305067737?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2305067737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15895211184362859531"><b>Well this is just a brilliant story that gave me far too many emotions.</b> Honestly I'm just feeling <i>all the things</i> and I didn't expect less from the queen Tahereh Mafi!! ajfsdklad I know this book is hugely drawn on from personal experience and just walking in Shirin's shoes, with the micro-aggressions (and the outright huge racist and xenophobic actions from people around her) and her hate of school and aching fear of wanting to love but not wanting to be hurt...it's an important story.<br/><br/>And I am j</span>
  <span id="freeText15895211184362859531" style="display:none"><b>Well this is just a brilliant story that gave me far too many emotions.</b> Honestly I'm just feeling <i>all the things</i> and I didn't expect less from the queen Tahereh Mafi!! ajfsdklad I know this book is hugely drawn on from personal experience and just walking in Shirin's shoes, with the micro-aggressions (and the outright huge racist and xenophobic actions from people around her) and her hate of school and aching fear of wanting to love but not wanting to be hurt...it's an important story.<br /><br />And I am just a smeeeeear of feels upon the floor thanks.<br /><br />➸ <b>Smallest thing I was sad about: </b>I missed Mafi's whimsical, flowery writing! This was a straight-forward tone, with Shirin being very no-nonsense. But it's also awesome to see authors conquer a wide variety of styles so !! (And I did feel the last 20% fell into telling instead of...well <i>showing</i> . I prefer to be IN the event, not recaped?)<br /><br />➸ <b> BUT WOW CAN WE TALK ABOUT SHIRIN.</b> I freaking loved her. She is like a snarky thorn bush and I just wish to leave her and Ronan (from The Raven Cycle) in a room together so they could both say, "I am being perfectly fucking civil" together. Because this is entire Shirin Mood. She is a burnt marshmallow and I JUST LOVED HER. And just seeing what her life was like was so sobering. She's abused for wearing hijab (it's set in 2002) and treated like trash, she's been attacked on the street, kids are awful to her in school, plus she moves a lot. <b>She definitely showed signs of a lot of depression.</b> She is just <i>surviving</i>. That's it.<br /><br />...and then she discovers both:<br />➸ breakdancing! she and her (epic) brother Navid start a club with 3 of his friends and this is wholesome badass dancing goodness<br />➸ Ocean! an actual boy, not the sea! who is quiet and soft and awkward and has a desperate crush on her and makes mistakes but <i>wants to learn to do better</i> and has really pretty eyessssss<br /><br />And just seeing Shirin having to work through her terror of being hurt (and eventually she worries about Ocean getting hurt) and then the unraveling chain of horrible events just because thESE TWO KIDS WANT TO BE HAPPY TOGETHER ahhhhhhh<br /><br />[extended sob]<br /><br />It's so well written. It's powerful and heartwrenching and there are many many fun and uplifting moments to balance ones where you're livid with rage that anyone would dare hurt Shirin. And I also just freaking LOVED reading about breakdancing. (I know nothing lmao. But there is a move called the Cricket and I know that now.) And Navid was a Good Brother and I appreciate his existence immensely.<br /><br /><b>Anyway: READ THIS.</b> I've officially read 6 Mafi books this year (some rereads) and my heart is very full.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15895211184362859531" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2584850855?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah Greendale" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale">Hannah Greendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=national-book-award-nominee">national-book-award-nominee</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2584850855" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1025802666116448945">Aside from a few short bursts of insight on a Muslim girl suffering racists microaggressions a year after 9/11, <i>A Very Large Expanse of Sea</i> is your average, run-of-the-mill coming-of-age YA romance featuring a teenager who hates school, laments life, is awkward around boys, doesn't understand her feelings for the first guy who's kind to her, etc., etc., etc. <br/><br/>Lots of telling; crucial moments that hold vast potential for tension and emotional depth are glossed over in brief recap. One male charact</span>
  <span id="freeText1025802666116448945" style="display:none">Aside from a few short bursts of insight on a Muslim girl suffering racists microaggressions a year after 9/11, <i>A Very Large Expanse of Sea</i> is your average, run-of-the-mill coming-of-age YA romance featuring a teenager who hates school, laments life, is awkward around boys, doesn't understand her feelings for the first guy who's kind to her, etc., etc., etc. <br /><br />Lots of telling; crucial moments that hold vast potential for tension and emotional depth are glossed over in brief recap. One male character's physically violent outbursts are never addressed. The conclusion is realistic yet unsatisfying. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>"You sound so sleepy." <br /><br />"Yeah," he said quietly. "I don't know. I'm tired, but I feel so happy." <br /><br />"You do?" <br /><br />"Yeah," he whispered. "You make me so happy." He took a deep breath. Laughed a little. "You're like a happy drug." <br /><br />I was smiling. I didn't know what to say. <br /><br />"You there?" <br /><br />"Yeah," I said. "I'm here." <br /><br />"What are you thinking?"<br /><br />"I'm thinking I wish you were here." <br /><br />"Yeah?" <br /><br />"Yeah," I said. "That'd be great."</i>
</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_2683644721" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2683644721" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2683644721?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tatiana by: </span>
      book club
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2">2</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=national-book-award">national-book-award</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=starred-2018">starred-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=romancelandia">romancelandia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2683644721" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7670271091353264576">2.5 stars, generously rounded up.<br/><br/>Islamophobia is terrible, but writing about it as a background to an overwrought, angsty, dull "Guys like you don't talk to girls like me" teen romance was an odd choice, IMO. It shifted the narrative's focus from Shirin's pain to her boyfriend's, making him the central recipient of hate. As a white woman married (for a long time, we met in 2003) to an Asian man who is in turns perceived as an "Arab" or "Mexican," depending on the preferred hated racial group of </span>
  <span id="freeText7670271091353264576" style="display:none">2.5 stars, generously rounded up.<br /><br />Islamophobia is terrible, but writing about it as a background to an overwrought, angsty, dull "Guys like you don't talk to girls like me" teen romance was an odd choice, IMO. It shifted the narrative's focus from Shirin's pain to her boyfriend's, making him the central recipient of hate. As a white woman married (for a long time, we met in 2003) to an Asian man who is in turns perceived as an "Arab" or "Mexican," depending on the preferred hated racial group of the assholes who find it acceptable to harass him at work or in the world, I can assure you, I am not the one who suffers in this equation, it's him. And in this story it should be Shirin.<br /><br />I think maybe this strange imbalance has something to do with they way this story is written. Those who point to all tell, no show, mean that this book mostly reads like a long recap of things happening in Shirin's life. The story only stops and happens in real time during the inane conversations with the boyfriend, making those moments seem the most important, when they just aren't. Shirin is abused for her faith and for belonging to a certain culture, and yet so little page space is given to those subjects. We rarely spend time with her wonderful family (the only time they have an opportunity to shine is during a dinner when THE BOYFRIEND shows up) or her breakdance buddies (I find it hard to believe they wouldn't have stood up for her) or other minority teens at that school. They barely exist in the story. The only things that do exist are Ocean with his pretty eyes, and hate. And I needed more of Shirin and her world. <br /><br />A story that could have been more if it wasn’t so fixated on a boy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7670271091353264576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2692952176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8618723044362834105"><b> “I didn't believe it was possible to hide a woman's beauty. I thought women were gorgeous no matter what they wore, and I didn't think they owed anyone an explanation for their sartorial choices. Different women felt comfortable in different outfits.<br/>They were all beautiful.” <br/>― Tahereh Mafi, A Very Large Expanse of Sea</b><br/><br/>This was a buddy read with my beautiful friend <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/82037192-imane' rel='nofollow noopener'>Imane</a>.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548704828i/26982275._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='270' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I wanted to like this, really wanted to and I did enjoy the writing style and the cute romance but my biggest problem was Shiri</span>
  <span id="freeText8618723044362834105" style="display:none"><b> “I didn't believe it was possible to hide a woman's beauty. I thought women were gorgeous no matter what they wore, and I didn't think they owed anyone an explanation for their sartorial choices. Different women felt comfortable in different outfits.<br>They were all beautiful.” <br>― Tahereh Mafi, A Very Large Expanse of Sea</b><br><br>This was a buddy read with my beautiful friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/82037192-imane" rel="nofollow noopener">Imane</a>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548704828i/26982275._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I wanted to like this, really wanted to and I did enjoy the writing style and the cute romance but my biggest problem was Shirin, I've never read a book with a Muslim as a main character before, and as a Muslim girl myself, I thought that maybe I could relate to her ... but no, Shirin was so weird and angry, always complaining, she hated her school and lamented her life...<br>Okay, I get it. It sucks to be bullied because of how you choose to dress, but for me, Tahereh completely missed the chance to delve deeper into the experience of a Muslim teenager in a post-9/11 world. Many of the most interesting elements are glossed over, I expected much more than just a story about bullies and break dancing practices. I also felt that the ending was a bit rushed!<br>Oh, and btw i totally disagree with the author, hijab and headscarf are not the same thing, but this is a completely different discussion, if you want to learn more, you can check out <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_J5bDhMP9lQ" rel="nofollow noopener">this amazing Ted talk by Samina Ali </a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10612711499215171495">I’m a white girl. I know the privilege the color of my skin gives me. <br/>Sometimes people stare at me, I can feel their eyes on me while crossing the street. It happens once in a lifetime and it gives me shivers. I don’t know why they do it, but I know they aren’t commenting the color of my skin, they are not assuming my culture or my religion. I don’t get racist comments, never had, never will. <br/><br/>This book was a punch in the stomach. <br/>And if it was a punch in the stomach for me, a girl who never has </span>
  <span id="freeText10612711499215171495" style="display:none">I’m a white girl. I know the privilege the color of my skin gives me. <br />Sometimes people stare at me, I can feel their eyes on me while crossing the street. It happens once in a lifetime and it gives me shivers. I don’t know why they do it, but I know they aren’t commenting the color of my skin, they are not assuming my culture or my religion. I don’t get racist comments, never had, never will. <br /><br />This book was a punch in the stomach. <br />And if it was a punch in the stomach for me, a girl who never has gone through what shirin has, I can’t imagine what a massive gigantic kick in the stomach was for all of you who not only understand her story, but are actually living what she is daily.<br />I’m sorry.<br />I’m grateful Tahereh decided to write this story.<br />I’m happy she did it for each one of you who is going through all of this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10612711499215171495" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
